   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">International Tennis Federation</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> 
    <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> 
    <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">

        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The <b>International Tennis Federation</b> (<b>ITF</b>) is the <a href="/wiki/Sports_governing_body" title="Sports governing body">governing body</a> of world <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheelchair_tennis" title="Wheelchair tennis">wheelchair tennis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Beach_tennis" title="Beach tennis">beach tennis</a>. It was founded in 1913 as the International Lawn Tennis Federation by twelve national associations, and as of 2016, is affiliated with 211 <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_tennis_associations" title="List of national tennis associations">national tennis associations</a> and six regional associations. </p>
      <p>The ITF's governance responsibilities include maintaining and enforcing the rules of tennis, regulating international team competitions, promoting the game, and preserving the sport's integrity via anti-doping and anti-corruption programs. The ITF partners with the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Tennis_Association" title="Women's Tennis Association">Women's Tennis Association</a> (WTA) and the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Tennis_Professionals" title="Association of Tennis Professionals">Association of Tennis Professionals</a> (ATP) to govern professional tennis. </p>
      <p>The ITF organizes the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam events</a>, annual team competitions for men (<a href="/wiki/Davis_Cup" title="Davis Cup">Davis Cup</a>), women (<a href="/wiki/Fed_Cup" title="Fed Cup">Fed Cup</a>), and mixed teams (<a href="/wiki/Hopman_Cup" title="Hopman Cup">Hopman Cup</a>), as well as tennis and wheelchair tennis events at the <a href="/wiki/Tennis_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="Tennis at the Summer Olympics">Summer Olympic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wheelchair_tennis_at_the_Summer_Paralympics" title="Wheelchair tennis at the Summer Paralympics">Paralympic</a> Games on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a>. The ITF sanctions the Grand Slam tennis tournaments as well as circuits which span age ranges (<a href="/wiki/ITF_Junior_Circuit" title="ITF Junior Circuit">junior</a>, professional <a href="/wiki/ITF_Men%27s_Circuit" title="ITF Men's Circuit">men</a> and <a href="/wiki/ITF_Women%27s_Circuit" title="ITF Women's Circuit">women</a>, and seniors) as well as disciplines (<a href="/wiki/ITF_Wheelchair_Tennis_Tour" title="ITF Wheelchair Tennis Tour">wheelchair tennis</a>; <a href="/wiki/ITF_Beach_Tennis_Tour" title="ITF Beach Tennis Tour">beach tennis</a>). In addition to these circuits, the ITF also maintains rankings for juniors, seniors, wheelchair and beach tennis. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Duane_Williams" title="Duane Williams">Duane Williams</a>, an American who lived in Switzerland, is generally recognized as the initiator and driving force behind the foundation of the International Tennis Federation. He died in the sinking of the <a href="/wiki/RMS_Titanic" title="RMS Titanic">RMS&nbsp;<i>Titanic</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gillmeister1998_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gillmeister1998-2">[2]</a></sup> Originally called the <b>International Lawn Tennis Federation</b> (ILTF) it held its inaugural conference at the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Union_des_Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9s_Fran%C3%A7aises_de_Sports_Athl%C3%A9tiques" title="Union des Sociétés Françaises de Sports Athlétiques">Union des Sociétés Françaises de Sports Athlétiques</a> (USFSA), in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> on 1 March 1913 which was attended by 12 national associations. Three other countries could not attend but had requested to become a member.<sup id="cite_ref-foundingmembers_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foundingmembers-3">[a]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup> Voting rights were divided based on the perceived importance of the individual countries with Great Britain's <a href="/wiki/Lawn_Tennis_Association" title="Lawn Tennis Association">Lawn Tennis Association</a> (LTA) receiving the maximum six votes.<sup id="cite_ref-gillmeister1998_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gillmeister1998-2">[2]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The LTA was given the perpetual right to organize the <a href="/wiki/Wimbledon_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="Wimbledon Championships">World Grass Championships</a> which led to a refusal by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Lawn_Tennis_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Lawn Tennis Association">United States Lawn Tennis Association</a> (USLTA) to join the ILTF as they were of the opinion that this title should be given to the <a href="/wiki/Davis_Cup" title="Davis Cup">Davis Cup</a>. France received permission to stage the <a href="/wiki/World_Hard_Court_Championships" title="World Hard Court Championships">World Hard Court Championships</a> until 1916 and additionally a <a href="/wiki/World_Covered_Court_Championships" title="World Covered Court Championships">World Covered Court Championships</a> was founded.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBowers201318–20_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBowers201318–20-6">[5]</a></sup> The USLTA joined in 1923 on the basis of two compromises: the title 'World Championships' would be abolished and wording would be 'for ever in the English language'.<sup id="cite_ref-gillmeister1998_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gillmeister1998-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EOT_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EOT-7">[6]</a></sup> The World Championships were replaced by a new category of Official Championships for the main tournaments in Australia, France, Great Britain and the United States; now known as the four Majors or Grand Slam events. In 1924, the ILTF became the officially recognised organisation with authority to control <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">lawn tennis</a> throughout the world, with official <i>ILTF Rules of Tennis</i>. </p>
      <p>In 1939 the ILTF had 59 member nations. Its funds were moved to London, England during World War II and from that time onward the ITF has been run from there. It was based at <a href="/wiki/Wimbledon,_London" title="Wimbledon, London">Wimbledon</a> until 1987, when it moved to <a href="/wiki/Barons_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="Barons Court">Barons Court</a>, next door to <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Club" title="Queen's Club">Queen's Club</a>. It then moved again in 1998 to the Bank of England Sports Ground, <a href="/wiki/Roehampton" title="Roehampton">Roehampton</a>, its current base of operations.<sup id="cite_ref-history_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1977 the word 'Lawn' was dropped from the name of the organization, in recognition of the fact that most tennis events were no longer played on <a href="/wiki/Grass_court" title="Grass court">grass</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Publications">Publications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Publications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Its official annual is <i><a href="/wiki/The_ITF_Year" title="The ITF Year">The ITF Year</a></i>, describing the activities of the ITF over last 12 months. This replaced <i><a href="/wiki/World_of_Tennis" title="World of Tennis">World of Tennis</a></i>, which was the ITF official annual from 1981 through 2001. In addition it publishes an official magazine <i>ITFWorld</i> three times a year. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:World_Map_ITF_Regions.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/89/World_Map_ITF_Regions.svg/400px-World_Map_ITF_Regions.svg.png" decoding="async" width="400" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/89/World_Map_ITF_Regions.svg/600px-World_Map_ITF_Regions.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/89/World_Map_ITF_Regions.svg/800px-World_Map_ITF_Regions.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="940" data-file-height="415"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:World_Map_ITF_Regions.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of the world showing countries whose national tennis associations are ITF members. Colors indicate the six regional associations.
        </div>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_and_Regional_Associations">National and Regional Associations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: National and Regional Associations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>As of 2017, there are 211 <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_tennis_associations" title="List of national tennis associations">national associations</a> affiliated with the ITF, of which 148 are voting members and 63 are associate members.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup> The criteria for allocating votes (1, 3, 5, 7, 9, or 12) to each voting member are: performance in ITF team competitions; professional (ATP/WTA), junior, and wheelchair rankings of individuals; track record in organizing international tournaments; and contribution to ITF infrastructure. For example, <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Fran%C3%A7aise_de_Tennis" class="mw-redirect" title="Fédération Française de Tennis">France</a> garners 12 votes, <a href="/wiki/Tennis_Canada" title="Tennis Canada">Canada</a> has 9, <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Tennis_Federation" title="Egyptian Tennis Federation">Egypt</a> has 5, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Tennis_Federation" title="Pakistan Tennis Federation">Pakistan</a> has 3, and <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Tennis_Association" title="Botswana Tennis Association">Botswana</a> has 1 vote.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEITF_Constitution201644-49_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEITF_Constitution201644-49-9">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Regional associations were created in July 1975 as six "supra-national associations" (Europe, Asia, Africa, North America, South America, and Australia) with the aim to decrease the gap between the ILTF and the national associations. These evolved into the current regional associations:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBowers201326_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBowers201326-10">[9]</a></sup> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span style="background-color:#669966; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span> 
        <a href="/wiki/Asian_Tennis_Federation" title="Asian Tennis Federation">Asian Tennis Federation</a> (ATF) – 44 members
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        <span style="background-color:#FF9999; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span> 
        <a href="/wiki/Central_American_%26_Caribbean_Tennis_Confederation" title="Central American &amp; Caribbean Tennis Confederation">Central American &amp; Caribbean Tennis Confederation</a> (COTECC) – 33 members
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        <span style="background-color:#CC9900; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span> 
        <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Tennis" title="Confederation of African Tennis">Confederation of African Tennis</a> (CAT) – 52 members
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        <span style="background-color:#996699; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span> 
        <a href="/wiki/Oceania_Tennis_Federation" title="Oceania Tennis Federation">Oceania Tennis Federation</a> (OTF) – 20 members
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        <span style="background-color:#99CCCC; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span> 
        <a href="/wiki/South_America_Tennis_Confederation" title="South America Tennis Confederation">South America Tennis Confederation</a> (COSAT) – 10 members
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        <span style="background-color:#CC6666; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span> 
        <a href="/wiki/Tennis_Europe" title="Tennis Europe">Tennis Europe</a> (TE) – 50 members
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        <span style="background-color:#99CC00; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span> ITF members with no regional affiliation (Canada and United States)
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Board_of_Directors">Board of Directors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Board of Directors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The ITF President and Board of Directors are elected every four years by the national associations. Candidates are nominated by the national associations, and may serve up to twelve years.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The ITF is the world governing body for the sport of tennis. Its governance includes the following responsibilities: make, amend, and enforce the Rules of Tennis; regulate international team competitions; promote the game of tennis; and preserve the integrity of tennis. </p>
      <p>By its own constitution, the ITF guarantees that the official Rules of Tennis "shall be for ever in the English language".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEITF_Constitution201630_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEITF_Constitution201630-12">[11]</a></sup> A committee within the ITF periodically makes rule amendment recommendations to the Board of Directors. The Rules of Tennis encompass the manner of play and scoring, in-game coaching, and the technical specifications of equipment (e.g. ball, racket, net, court) and other technology (e.g. player analysis technology). The Rules cover tennis, wheelchair tennis, and beach tennis.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Through the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tennis_Anti-Doping_Program&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tennis Anti-Doping Program (page does not exist)">Tennis Anti-Doping Program</a>, the ITF implements the World Anti-Doping Code (from the <a href="/wiki/World_Anti-Doping_Agency" title="World Anti-Doping Agency">World Anti-Doping Agency</a>, or WADA) for tennis. National associations must implement the code within its national jurisdiction, report violations up to the ITF and WADA, and report annually about all testing conducted.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEITF_Constitution201639-40_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEITF_Constitution201639-40-14">[13]</a></sup> The Tennis Anti-Doping Program began in 1993, and applies to all players who play in ITF-sanctioned competitions, as well as tournaments on the <a href="/wiki/ATP_Tour" title="ATP Tour">ATP Tour</a> and <a href="/wiki/WTA_Tour" title="WTA Tour">WTA Tour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> In 2015, 2514 samples were collected from men and 1919 samples were collected from women; 2256 samples were collected during tennis tournaments ("in-competition") and 2177 were collected at other times ("out-of-competition").<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Tennis_Integrity_Unit" title="Tennis Integrity Unit">Tennis Integrity Unit</a> (TIU) is a joint initiative of the primary governing bodies in tennis: the ITF, the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Tennis_Professionals" title="Association of Tennis Professionals">Association of Tennis Professionals</a> (ATP), the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Tennis_Association" title="Women's Tennis Association">Women's Tennis Association</a> (WTA), and the Grand Slam Board. Formed in 2008 in response to betting-related corruption challenges, the TIU's mandate is to protect tennis from "all forms of betting-related corrupt practices".<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> As with the anti-doping efforts, national associations are charged with the responsibility of enforcing a code of conduct and reporting any violations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEITF_Constitution201640_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEITF_Constitution201640-18">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Competitions">Competitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Competitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_competitions">Team competitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Team competitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The ITF operates the two major annual international team competitions in the sport, the <a href="/wiki/Davis_Cup" title="Davis Cup">Davis Cup</a><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> for men, the <a href="/wiki/Fed_Cup" title="Fed Cup">Fed Cup</a><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> for women. It also sanctions the <a href="/wiki/Hopman_Cup" title="Hopman Cup">Hopman Cup</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> an annual mixed-gender team tournament. The ITF also organizes tennis and wheelchair tennis events every four years at the Summer Olympic and Paralympic Games on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Davis_Cup">Davis Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Davis Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vincent_Richards,_Bill_Tilden_and_Bill_Johnston_at_the_1922_Davis_Cup.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Vincent_Richards%2C_Bill_Tilden_and_Bill_Johnston_at_the_1922_Davis_Cup.jpg/220px-Vincent_Richards%2C_Bill_Tilden_and_Bill_Johnston_at_the_1922_Davis_Cup.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Vincent_Richards%2C_Bill_Tilden_and_Bill_Johnston_at_the_1922_Davis_Cup.jpg/330px-Vincent_Richards%2C_Bill_Tilden_and_Bill_Johnston_at_the_1922_Davis_Cup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Vincent_Richards%2C_Bill_Tilden_and_Bill_Johnston_at_the_1922_Davis_Cup.jpg/440px-Vincent_Richards%2C_Bill_Tilden_and_Bill_Johnston_at_the_1922_Davis_Cup.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4290" data-file-height="2909"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vincent_Richards,_Bill_Tilden_and_Bill_Johnston_at_the_1922_Davis_Cup.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Richards" title="Vincent Richards">Vincent Richards</a>, 
         <a href="/wiki/Bill_Tilden" title="Bill Tilden">Bill Tilden</a> and 
         <a href="/wiki/Bill_Johnston_(tennis)" title="Bill Johnston (tennis)">Bill Johnston</a> at the 
         <a href="/wiki/1922_Davis_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="1922 Davis Cup">1922 Davis Cup</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: 
       <a href="/wiki/Davis_Cup" title="Davis Cup">Davis Cup</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Davis Cup, named after its founder <a href="/wiki/Dwight_F._Davis" title="Dwight F. Davis">Dwight F. Davis</a>, is an annual team event organized by the ITF (since 1979 when it replaced the Committee of Davis Cup Nations as event organiser) <sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> in men's tennis contested between teams from competing countries in a <a href="/wiki/Single-elimination_tournament" title="Single-elimination tournament">knock-out</a> format. The first Davis Cup took place in 1900, prior to the formation of the ITF. Since 1981, the tournament has been divided into a 16-nation World Group, and zone groups (Americas; Europe/Africa; and Asia/Oceania) which compete in three or four tiers.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> Each year, successful teams are may be promoted up one level, while unsuccessful teams are relegated down one level. Davis Cup rounds are contested four times per year, scheduled to minimize disruption with the <a href="/wiki/ATP_Tour" title="ATP Tour">ATP Tour</a> to encourage participation. In each round, a combination of singles and doubles matches are contested to determine the winners. In 2016, 135 nations participated, making it the largest annual international team competition in sport.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fed_Cup">Fed Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Fed Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: 
       <a href="/wiki/Fed_Cup" title="Fed Cup">Fed Cup</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Petra_Kvitova_Fed_Cup_2011_Winner.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Petra_Kvitova_Fed_Cup_2011_Winner.jpg/220px-Petra_Kvitova_Fed_Cup_2011_Winner.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Petra_Kvitova_Fed_Cup_2011_Winner.jpg/330px-Petra_Kvitova_Fed_Cup_2011_Winner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Petra_Kvitova_Fed_Cup_2011_Winner.jpg/440px-Petra_Kvitova_Fed_Cup_2011_Winner.jpg 2x" data-file-width="717" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Petra_Kvitova_Fed_Cup_2011_Winner.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Petra_Kvitov%C3%A1" title="Petra Kvitová">Petra Kvitová</a>, a member of the winning 
         <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic_Fed_Cup_team" title="Czech Republic Fed Cup team">Czech Republic Fed Cup Team</a> in 2011
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Fed Cup is an annual team event organized by the ITF in women's tennis, similar in format to the Davis Cup. It was launched in 1963 to celebrate the 50th anniversary of the ITF. Since 2005, the tournament has been divided into an eight-nation World Group, an eight-nation World Group II, and zone groups (Americas; Europe/Africa; and Asia/Oceania) which compete in two or three tiers.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> Like the Davis Cup, the rules of promotion and relegation are almost the same each year, except that it contests World Group II, which does not exist in the Davis Cup. Fed Cup rounds are contested three times per year, scheduled to minimize disruption with the <a href="/wiki/WTA_Tour" title="WTA Tour">WTA Tour</a> to encourage participation. In each round, a combination of singles and doubles matches are contested to determine the winners. In 2016, 102 nations participated, making it the largest annual international team competition in women's sport.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hopman_Cup">Hopman Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Hopman Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: 
       <a href="/wiki/Hopman_Cup" title="Hopman Cup">Hopman Cup</a>
      </div>
      <p>The Hopman Cup is an annual team event which is contested by mixed-gender national teams. The first tournament was held in 1989, and the event has been sanctioned by the ITF since 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> The tournament is held over one week at the start of the tennis season (late December or early January) in Australia. Each year, eight nations are selected to compete, with one female and one male invited to attend. Two pools of four teams each play matches in a <a href="/wiki/Round-robin_tournament" title="Round-robin tournament">round-robin</a> format, with the top team from each pool qualifying for the final.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympics_and_Paralympics">Olympics and Paralympics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Olympics and Paralympics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: 
       <a href="/wiki/Tennis_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="Tennis at the Summer Olympics">Tennis at the Summer Olympics</a> and 
       <a href="/wiki/Wheelchair_tennis_at_the_Summer_Paralympics" title="Wheelchair tennis at the Summer Paralympics">Wheelchair tennis at the Summer Paralympics</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Azarenka,_Serena_Williams_and_Maria_Sharapova_with_medals_2012_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Victoria_Azarenka%2C_Serena_Williams_and_Maria_Sharapova_with_medals_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Victoria_Azarenka%2C_Serena_Williams_and_Maria_Sharapova_with_medals_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Victoria_Azarenka%2C_Serena_Williams_and_Maria_Sharapova_with_medals_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Victoria_Azarenka%2C_Serena_Williams_and_Maria_Sharapova_with_medals_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Victoria_Azarenka%2C_Serena_Williams_and_Maria_Sharapova_with_medals_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Victoria_Azarenka%2C_Serena_Williams_and_Maria_Sharapova_with_medals_2012_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="472" data-file-height="546"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Azarenka,_Serena_Williams_and_Maria_Sharapova_with_medals_2012_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Azarenka" title="Victoria Azarenka">Victoria Azarenka</a>, 
         <a href="/wiki/Serena_Williams" title="Serena Williams">Serena Williams</a>, and 
         <a href="/wiki/Maria_Sharapova" title="Maria Sharapova">Maria Sharapova</a> at the 
         <a href="/wiki/Tennis_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Tennis at the 2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Tennis (lawn tennis) was part of the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Summer Olympic Games</a> program from the inaugural <a href="/wiki/1896_Summer_Olympics" title="1896 Summer Olympics">1896 Summer Olympics</a>, but was dropped after the <a href="/wiki/1924_Summer_Olympics" title="1924 Summer Olympics">1924 Summer Olympics</a> due to disputes between the ITF and the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> over allowing amateur players to compete.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> After two appearances as a <a href="/wiki/Demonstration_sport" title="Demonstration sport">demonstration sport</a> in 1968 and 1984,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> it returned as a full medal sport at the <a href="/wiki/1988_Summer_Olympics" title="1988 Summer Olympics">1988 Summer Olympics</a> and has been played at every edition of the Games since then.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Wheelchair tennis was first contested at the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Paralympic_Games" title="Summer Paralympic Games">Summer Paralympic Games</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Demonstration_sport" title="Demonstration sport">demonstration sport</a> in 1988, with two events being held (Men's and Women's Singles). It became an official medal-awarding sport in 1992 and has been competed at every Summer Paralympics since then. Four events were held from 1992 to 2000, with quad events (mixed gender) in both singles and doubles added in 2004. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Individual_competitions">Individual competitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Individual competitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The ITF sanctions the Grand Slam tennis tournaments as well as circuits which span age ranges (junior, professional, and seniors) as well as disciplines (<a href="/wiki/Wheelchair_tennis" title="Wheelchair tennis">wheelchair tennis</a>; <a href="/wiki/Beach_tennis" title="Beach tennis">beach tennis</a>). In addition to these circuits, the ITF also maintains rankings for juniors, seniors, wheelchair, and beach tennis. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_Slam_tournaments">Grand Slam tournaments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Grand Slam tournaments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: 
       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam (tennis)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The ITF organizes and sanctions the 'Official Tennis Championships of the International Tennis Federation', commonly known as the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> events: the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Open" title="Australian Open">Australian Open</a>, the <a href="/wiki/French_Open" title="French Open">French Open</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Championships,_Wimbledon" title="The Championships, Wimbledon">Wimbledon</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/US_Open_(tennis)" title="US Open (tennis)">US Open</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> It is a member of the Grand Slam Committee.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_circuit">Professional circuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Professional circuit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: 
       <a href="/wiki/ITF_Men%27s_Circuit" title="ITF Men's Circuit">ITF Men's Circuit</a> and 
       <a href="/wiki/ITF_Women%27s_Circuit" title="ITF Women's Circuit">ITF Women's Circuit</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The ITF organizes introductory ("apprentice" level) professional circuits for both men and women as a bridge between junior tournaments and playing on the higher-profile tours organized by the ATP and WTA, respectively. Professional circuit tournaments are open to all tennis players aged 14 and over based on merit, and offer both prize money and world ranking points for main draw match victories. The tournaments are owned or sanctioned by the national associations and approved by the ITF.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although circuits were introduced to men's tennis in 1976, the ITF assumed responsibility for developing them in 1990. From then until 2006, four-week <a href="/wiki/Satellite_tournaments" class="mw-redirect" title="Satellite tournaments">satellite tournaments</a> were run, where participants were required to compete in the entire series. In 1998, single-week ITF Futures tournaments were introduced, although they are scheduled in two or three-week geographic clusters.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> As of 2016, over 600 ITF Futures tournaments in 77 countries were held, with prize funds ranging from USD 10,000 to USD 25,000.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-37">[36]</a></sup> ITF Futures tournaments represent the third tier of men's tournaments, below the mid-level <a href="/wiki/ATP_Challenger_Tour" title="ATP Challenger Tour">ATP Challenger Tour</a> and the top-level <a href="/wiki/ATP_World_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="ATP World Tour">ATP World Tour</a>. </p>
      <p>The ITF assumed responsibility for an apprentice-level women's circuit in 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> As of 2016, the ITF women's circuit includes over 500 tournaments in 65 countries, with prize funds ranging from USD 10,000 to USD 100,000.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-37">[36]</a></sup> The ITF women's circuit is the third tier in women's tennis, below the mid-level <a href="/wiki/WTA_125K_series" title="WTA 125K series">WTA 125K series</a> and the top-level <a href="/wiki/WTA_Tour" title="WTA Tour">WTA Tour</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Junior_circuit">Junior circuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Junior circuit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: 
       <a href="/wiki/ITF_Junior_Circuit" title="ITF Junior Circuit">ITF Junior Circuit</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Filip_Peliwo_(CAN)_2012_US_Open.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Filip_Peliwo_%28CAN%29_2012_US_Open.jpg/220px-Filip_Peliwo_%28CAN%29_2012_US_Open.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Filip_Peliwo_%28CAN%29_2012_US_Open.jpg/330px-Filip_Peliwo_%28CAN%29_2012_US_Open.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Filip_Peliwo_%28CAN%29_2012_US_Open.jpg/440px-Filip_Peliwo_%28CAN%29_2012_US_Open.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2745" data-file-height="2122"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Filip_Peliwo_(CAN)_2012_US_Open.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Filip_Peliwo" title="Filip Peliwo">Filip Peliwo</a>, ITF Junior World Champion 2012, during the 
         <a href="/wiki/2012_US_Open_%E2%80%93_Boys%27_Singles" title="2012 US Open – Boys' Singles">2012 Junior US Open</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Starting in 1977, the ITF has organized a series of international tennis tournaments for junior players.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> Tournaments have various grades: Grade A (the highest; junior Grand Slams and some others), Grade 1, Grade 2, Grade 3, Grade 4, and Grade 5 (the lowest). Depending on the grade of tournament, players earn points toward the ITF Junior World Rankings. In 2004, the ITF introduced combined junior rankings rather than maintaining separate singles and doubles rankings for juniors in an effort to encourage doubles play.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> As of 2015, the junior circuit includes 400 tournaments in 121 countries, open to players who are between their 13th and 19th birthdays. </p>
      <p>In order to help high-ranking junior girls transition from the junior circuit to the professional circuit, the ITF began the Girls Junior Exempt Project in 1997. Under this program, girls ranked in the top 10 at the end of the year are given direct entry into the main draw of three events on the ITF professional circuit the following year. In 2006, this project was extended for boys under similar rules.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Seniors_circuit">Seniors circuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Seniors circuit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>As of 2016, the ITF Seniors Circuit consists of over 380 tournaments in more than 72 countries. Tournaments are classified into various grades, with Grade A being the highest and Grade 5 being the lowest. Rankings are maintained in a series of age groups where the starting ages advance five years at a time (e.g. 35 years and older; 40 years and older) up to the 85 years and older group.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> World championships began in 1981. In 1993, the world championships were divided into two age ranges, and in 2015 it was further divided into three age ranges. As of 2015, the ranges are Young Seniors (35 to 49); Seniors (50 to 64); and Super-Seniors (65 to 85).<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Wheelchair_circuit">Wheelchair circuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Wheelchair circuit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: 
       <a href="/wiki/ITF_Wheelchair_Tennis_Tour" title="ITF Wheelchair Tennis Tour">ITF Wheelchair Tennis Tour</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Aniek_van_Koot_(NED)_(21010874494).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Aniek_van_Koot_%28NED%29_%2821010874494%29.jpg/220px-Aniek_van_Koot_%28NED%29_%2821010874494%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Aniek_van_Koot_%28NED%29_%2821010874494%29.jpg/330px-Aniek_van_Koot_%28NED%29_%2821010874494%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Aniek_van_Koot_%28NED%29_%2821010874494%29.jpg/440px-Aniek_van_Koot_%28NED%29_%2821010874494%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3118" data-file-height="2411"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Aniek_van_Koot_(NED)_(21010874494).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Aniek_van_Koot" title="Aniek van Koot">Aniek van Koot</a> at the 
         <a href="/wiki/2015_US_Open_(tennis)" title="2015 US Open (tennis)">2015 US Open</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The first circuit for <a href="/wiki/Wheelchair_tennis" title="Wheelchair tennis">wheelchair tennis</a>, formed in 1980 by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=National_Foundation_of_Wheelchair_Tennis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="National Foundation of Wheelchair Tennis (page does not exist)">National Foundation of Wheelchair Tennis</a>, had ten tournaments. Beginning in 1992, the Wheelchair Tennis Tour began with eleven events, organized by the International Wheelchair Tennis Federation (IWTF) which merged with the ITF six years later.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> As of 2016, the wheelchair tennis circuit includes over 160 events in over 40 countries. This includes tournaments ranging from Futures (the lowest level) up to the Grand Slams.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Beach_tennis_circuit">Beach tennis circuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Beach tennis circuit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: 
       <a href="/wiki/ITF_Beach_Tennis_Tour" title="ITF Beach Tennis Tour">ITF Beach Tennis Tour</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:NYLB08_3620.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/NYLB08_3620.jpg/220px-NYLB08_3620.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/NYLB08_3620.jpg/330px-NYLB08_3620.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/NYLB08_3620.jpg/440px-NYLB08_3620.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="360"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:NYLB08_3620.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Beach tennis match
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2008, the ITF assumed responsibility for the development of beach tennis and launched the Beach Tennis Tour (BTT). This tour started with 14 tournaments, but has grown to nearly 300 tournaments by 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> The most prestigious of these are the ITF Beach Tennis World Team Championship, ITF Beach Tennis World Championships, European Beach Tennis Championships, and the ITF Pan American Championships.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> Like the other ITF circuits, tournaments are sanctioned by the ITF and primarily organized by national associations. The ITF also maintains a system of rankings for beach tennis players.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_rankings">Awards and rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Awards and rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Roger_Federer_and_Serena_Williams_Annual_International_Tennis_Federation_World_Champion_Trophies_by_sculptor_Laurence_Broderick.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Roger_Federer_and_Serena_Williams_Annual_International_Tennis_Federation_World_Champion_Trophies_by_sculptor_Laurence_Broderick.jpg/220px-Roger_Federer_and_Serena_Williams_Annual_International_Tennis_Federation_World_Champion_Trophies_by_sculptor_Laurence_Broderick.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="321" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Roger_Federer_and_Serena_Williams_Annual_International_Tennis_Federation_World_Champion_Trophies_by_sculptor_Laurence_Broderick.jpg/330px-Roger_Federer_and_Serena_Williams_Annual_International_Tennis_Federation_World_Champion_Trophies_by_sculptor_Laurence_Broderick.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Roger_Federer_and_Serena_Williams_Annual_International_Tennis_Federation_World_Champion_Trophies_by_sculptor_Laurence_Broderick.jpg/440px-Roger_Federer_and_Serena_Williams_Annual_International_Tennis_Federation_World_Champion_Trophies_by_sculptor_Laurence_Broderick.jpg 2x" data-file-width="686" data-file-height="1000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roger_Federer_and_Serena_Williams_Annual_International_Tennis_Federation_World_Champion_Trophies_by_sculptor_Laurence_Broderick.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>2009 ITF World Champion trophies awarded to 
         <a href="/wiki/Roger_Federer" title="Roger Federer">Roger Federer</a> and 
         <a href="/wiki/Serena_Williams" title="Serena Williams">Serena Williams</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_champions">World champions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: World champions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: 
       <a href="/wiki/ITF_World_Champions" title="ITF World Champions">ITF World Champions</a>
      </div>
      <p>The ITF designates a World Champion in several disciplines each year based on performances throughout the year, emphasizing the Grand Slam tournaments, and also considering team events such as the Davis Cup and Fed Cup. Singles champions were first named in 1978, and are chosen by an ITF panel. In later years, World Champion awards were added for doubles, juniors (using a combined singles and doubles ranking), and wheelchair players.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEITF_Constitution201636,38_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEITF_Constitution201636,38-49">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although the panel selections generally agree with the year-end <a href="/wiki/ATP_Rankings" title="ATP Rankings">ATP</a> and <a href="/wiki/WTA_Rankings" title="WTA Rankings">WTA</a> rankings, this is not always the case. For example, <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Capriati" title="Jennifer Capriati">Jennifer Capriati</a> was designated as the World Champion in 2001, after winning the Australian Open and French Open and finishing the year ranked number two. <a href="/wiki/Lindsay_Davenport" title="Lindsay Davenport">Lindsay Davenport</a>, on the other hand, finished the year ranked number one, but her best performances at majors were two semifinal appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_rankings">National rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: National rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: 
       <a href="/wiki/ITF_Rankings" title="ITF Rankings">ITF Rankings</a>
      </div>
      <p>The ITF maintains rankings of nations in both women's<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> and men's<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup> tennis based solely on recent performances in the Fed Cup and Davis Cup, respectively. These rankings are used to seed teams at the start of each year in their respective groups. </p>
      <p>The women's and men's rankings are calculated using a similar method.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> In both cases, a nation's points are a weighted sum of points earned over the past four years. Points are earned by victorious nations depending on the group (e.g. World Group versus Zonal Groups), the round (e.g. final versus first round), and the ranking of the opponent being played. For the men's ranking only, additional bonus points are awarded for winning on an opponent's home ground. Points earned in the last 12 months are weighted at 100%, but points earned two years (75%), three years (50%), and four years (25%) ago are weighted less. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Player_rating_and_registration">Player rating and registration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Player rating and registration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ITN">ITN</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: ITN">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <i>International Tennis Number</i> (ITN)<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> is an international tennis rating system that gives tennis players a number that represents their general level of play. Players are rated from ITN 1 (ATP or WTA standard or equivalent) to 10 (starter players). </p>
      <p>Conversion charts have been developed linking the ITN to other existing rating systems in ITF tennis nations and in time it is hoped that every tennis player worldwide will have a rating. </p>
      <p>Below ITN 10 there are 3 further categories linked to the slower balls: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>10.1 for players using green balls on the full-size court</li> 
       <li>10.2 for players using orange balls on the 18 metre court</li> 
       <li>10.3 for players using red balls on the 11 metre court</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Once players can ‘serve, rally and score’ they should have a rating to help them find players of a similar level to play with. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IPIN">IPIN</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: IPIN">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In late 2004 the ITF initiated a new IPIN (International Player Identification Number) programme that requires all players who play in ITF Pro Circuit tournaments to register online.<sup id="cite_ref-sbus_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sbus-56">[55]</a></sup> The use of IPIN has since been extended to include the ITF Junior, Seniors, and Wheelchair Circuits. A player's IPIN, which is 3 letters followed by 7 numbers, is assigned upon registration and will not change during the course of his or her career. Once registered, players can use the IPIN website to enter and withdraw from ITF tournaments, access tournament information and updates, and see details relating to any code of conduct offenses.<sup id="cite_ref-ipin2_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipin2-57">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ipin3_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipin3-58">[57]</a></sup> Annual IPIN registration fees vary depending on the ITF circuit chosen by the player. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fine_of_the_Tunisian_Tennis_Federation">Fine of the Tunisian Tennis Federation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Fine of the Tunisian Tennis Federation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Tunisian player <a href="/wiki/Malek_Jaziri" title="Malek Jaziri">Malek Jaziri</a> and Israeli player <a href="/wiki/Amir_Weintraub" title="Amir Weintraub">Amir Weintraub</a> were scheduled to play each other at the <a href="/wiki/2013_Tashkent_Challenger" title="2013 Tashkent Challenger">2013 Tashkent Challenger</a> in October 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-skysports1_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-skysports1-59">[58]</a></sup> Jaziri withdrew from the competition in January 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-skysports1_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-skysports1-59">[58]</a></sup> According to Jaziri's brother, Jaziri had been ordered to withdraw from the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-skysports1_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-skysports1-59">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Tennis_Professionals" title="Association of Tennis Professionals">Association of Tennis Professionals</a> investigated and found that Jaziri had done nothing wrong and that the Tunisian Tennis Federation's interference with the game had constituted a breach of the ITF Constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-skysports1_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-skysports1-59">[58]</a></sup> Consequently, Tunisia was suspended from the <a href="/wiki/2014_Davis_Cup" title="2014 Davis Cup">2014 Davis Cup</a> competition.<sup id="cite_ref-skysports1_59-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-skysports1-59">[58]</a></sup> ITF president <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Ricci_Bitti" title="Francesco Ricci Bitti">Francesco Ricci Bitti</a> said, "There is no room for prejudice of any kind in sport or in society. The ITF Board decided to send a strong message to the Tunisian Tennis Federation that this kind of action will not be tolerated."<sup id="cite_ref-skysports1_59-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-skysports1-59">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fine_of_the_Israel_Tennis_Association">Fine of the Israel Tennis Association</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Tennis_Federation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Fine of the Israel Tennis Association">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>A <a href="/wiki/Davis_Cup" title="Davis Cup">Davis Cup</a> game between the Israeli national tennis team and the Belgian national tennis team was scheduled in <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> for 14 September 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-sittingout_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sittingout-60">[59]</a></sup> Because the match was scheduled for <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur" title="Yom Kippur">Yom Kippur</a>, the Israeli team requested to postpone the match by one day.<sup id="cite_ref-sittingout_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sittingout-60">[59]</a></sup> The Belgian national tennis team declined to postpone the game.<sup id="cite_ref-sittingout_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sittingout-60">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The International Tennis Federation intervened and postponed the match by one day.<sup id="cite_ref-sittingout_60-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sittingout-60">[59]</a></sup> It also fined the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Tennis_Association" title="Israel Tennis Association">Israel Tennis Association</a> more than $13,000 for the inconvenience of rescheduling.<sup id="cite_ref-sittingout_60-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sittingout-60">[59]</a></sup> </p>
